  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7c258b9a-dd3f-4de0-9187-e46ebb441c2f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer8530667284046747987">Rosemary Bliss’s family has a secret. It’s the Bliss Cookery Booke—an ancient, leather-bound volume of enchanted recipes like Stone Sleep Snickerdoodles and Singing Gingersnaps.   <span id="freeText8530667284046747987" style="display:none">Rosemary Bliss’s family has a secret. It’s the Bliss Cookery Booke—an ancient, leather-bound volume of enchanted recipes like Stone Sleep Snickerdoodles and Singing Gingersnaps. Rose and her siblings are supposed to keep the Cookery Booke under lock and whisk-shaped key while their parents are out of town, but then a mysterious stranger shows up. “Aunt” Lily rides a motorcycle, wears purple sequins, and whips up exotic (but delicious) dishes for dinner. Soon boring, non-magical recipes feel like life before Aunt Lily—a lot less fun.<br /><br />So Rose and her siblings experiment with just a couple of recipes from the forbidden Cookery Booke.<br /><br />A few Love Muffins and a few dozen Cookies of Truth couldn’t cause too much trouble . . . could they?<br /><br />Kathryn Littlewood’s culinary caper blends rich emotional flavor with truly magical wit, yielding one heaping portion of hilarious family adventure.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/305586360?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookworm007" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookworm007" href="/user/show/2729265-bookworm007">Bookworm007</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062084231" href="/book/show/11595931-bliss">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who like low self-esteem protagonists</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305586360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17437050132082471250">LONG AND EXTENSIVE REVIEW WITH SEVERE CRITICISM<br/><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I reeeeally enjoyed this book. It had suspense and magic, and was easy to read. Reminds me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/232187.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory' title='Charlie and the Chocolate Factory by Roald Dahl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8112318.The_Candymakers' title='The Candymakers by Wendy Mass' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Candymakers</a>.<br/><br/><br/><br/>But I have to say, there were three things I didn’t like (possible spoilers):<br/><br/>1) Throughout the entire book, Rose had these stupid fantasies and just plain STUPID REMARKS about her crush and her.<br/><br/>She’d be like “Oh if we were boyfriend and girlfriend, we’d stand on top of the highest hill and look </span>
  <span id="freeText17437050132082471250" style="display:none">LONG AND EXTENSIVE REVIEW WITH SEVERE CRITICISM<br /><br /><br /><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />I reeeeally enjoyed this book. It had suspense and magic, and was easy to read. Reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/232187.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8112318.The_Candymakers" title="The Candymakers by Wendy Mass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Candymakers</a>.<br /><br /><br /><br />But I have to say, there were three things I didn’t like (possible spoilers):<br /><br />1) Throughout the entire book, Rose had these stupid fantasies and just plain STUPID REMARKS about her crush and her.<br /><br />She’d be like “Oh if we were boyfriend and girlfriend, we’d stand on top of the highest hill and look down at the town with the wind breezing about us” (like <i>that’s</i> romantic) or “I’M NOT PRETTY ENOUGH FOR HIM TO LIKE ME” or “I wanted to shove Love Muffins down his throat as fast as I can so he’d love me” or “I WANT HIM TO TAKE ME OUT ON A DATE <b>THIS INSTANT!!!</b>” or “He smells like soap and dreams” (who the FRICK smells like DREAMS) or “I’M NOT PRETTY ENOUGH FOR HIM TO LIKE ME!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!”<br /><br />If you asked me, that girl is friggin obSESSED with that guy, whatever his name is, (I think it was D something.) Like <i>hello</i> Rose, here’s a bright idea: Why don’t you actually take action and DO something about it, instead of having these ridiculous daydreams!!!<br /><br />You know, I actually thought that the guy would have a bigger role later in the book, and that whatever heroic deed he did, him and Rose would actually start to fall in love or whatever. (Cuz ain’t that what befalls almost every other “love-interest” guy in books these days.)<br /><br /><br />2) Rose is the most low-confidence girl EVER in the history of eternal EVER. She thinks everybody in the whole friggin universe outshines her. Like wtf is wrong with you, do you really think you sink that low? I mean, just because your older brother is Abercrombie &amp; Fitch gorgeous, doesn’t mean you aren’t (maybe you really aren’t, but whatev I just feel like criticizing you.)<br /><br />And she said she’s not pretty in almost <i><u>ev-ver-reeeee</u>. dang. chapter.</i> By the time fake-ass Aunt Lily gave her a makeover to make her PRETTY and BEAUTIFUL and GLAMOUROUS and SOMETHING TO LOOK AT, I was already pissed at this girl. And wanted to ring her neck. And shove her head down a toilet. And then chuck her down that stupid hilltop she favours so much.<br /><br />In short, Rose had serious self-esteem issues.<br /><br />(Well it’s no wonder her crush, D-something the other, hasn’t paid her much attention, HA!)<br /><br /><br />3) Aunt Lily. Sweet, beautiful, tall, supermodel Aunt Lily. The woman who waltzed into the Bliss siblings' life after their parents went away on some mission in Florida to cure a sickness. The woman who made Ty and Sage wanna help out in the bakery. The woman who was able to calm Chip’s grouchiness down. The woman who brought the siblings closer together. The woman who was caring and friendly. <s>The woman who outshined Rose by a million miles.</s> The woman who was supposed to have a <b>bigger antagonist role at the end of the book!!!!!!!!!!</b><br /><br />Myyyyyyy goodness, I can't express my disappointment enough.<br /><br />What I HOPED would happen was that Aunt Lily would drop her nicey-nice act and reveal her intentions for wanting the "Bliss Bakery Cook Booke", and her true identity. I HOPED there'd be a big secret bomb-shell. I HOPED her Bliss family ladle-shaped birthmark was fake. I HOPED all the siblings would've united together and take her down or something. I HOPED she'd use dark magic on the Bliss siblings. I HOPED a lot of things.<br /><br /><br />But nope, what really happened was this:<br /><br />Aunt Lily: Hey Rose, I'm leaving for New York and I need the Bliss Cook Booke for my tv show, so why don't you let me "borrow" it.<br /><br />Rose: Uh I'm not sure that's such a good idea...<br /><br />Aunt Lily: Ok, but just so you know, I outshine you by a million miles, and I think we all know that, so why don't you come along and I can make you shine like the brightest star in the sky.<br /><br />Rose: omgomgomgigettolookprettyandbeautifulomgomgomg<br /><br />Aunt Lily: Then it's settled. I'll make a "forgetful" bread for your family to eat. That way they won't remember you, me, and the cookbook.<br /><br />Rose: ...ok.....<br /><br />--the next day--<br /><br />Aunt Lily: Rose I'm gonna have to throw away that picture of your siblings in your hand cuz you have to forget them. -throws pic away-<br /><br />Rose: *finally has a clear mind* NO. I am not going away with you no more. -throws bag of "forgetful" bread in garbage can- You're a meanie, and even though my family will forget me, I won't be able to ever forget them.<br /><br />Aunt Lily: Fine, be that way. But I still outshine you by a million miles!! -leaves-with-cook-book-but-it-was-unknown-to-anyone-at-that-time-that-it-was-stolen-and-it-was-only-after-the-parents-came-home-that-everyone-found-out-which-left-Rose-saying-that-she-will-get-it-back-which-then-opened-up-the-possibility-of-a-sequel-<br /><br />THE END<br /><br /><br />If you were me, you'd probably be disappointed too. I was sooooo ready for a big showdown between the Bliss kids and Aunt Lily, but instead, THAT crap showed up. What the hell was the whole point of making Aunt Lily a dangerously-beautiful antagonist if NOT A CRAP HAPPENS AT THE END OF THE DANG BOOK.<br /><br />And goodness me, a possible sequel??? I seriously do not think I can stand another 300 or so pages of Rose internally screaming at herself for not being beautiful.<br /><br /><br /><br />Ok, deeeeep breathe.<br /><br />I've poured out all my criticism, and now I don't have the energy or enthusiasm to talk about what I actually enjoyed.<br /><br />-shrugs- Oh well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17437050132082471250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

But instead, she is always left out, and her brothers and her family don't seem to appreciate her. So, when her parents leave to take care of a town ailing wit</span>
  <span id="freeText18365246642504826516" style="display:none">So so disappointing. IT HAD SUCH A GOOD COVER AND PREMISE. <br />So, the premise of this is that Rose Bliss works at a magical bakery with her family. She is never allowed to touch the magic, though, and this irks her, because she knows she can make something special. She wants to make snickerdoodles that cure colds or cookies that warm hearts. But instead, she is always left out, and her brothers and her family don't seem to appreciate her. So, when her parents leave to take care of a town ailing with swine flu, and "Aunt" Lily shows up, she decides to take matters into her own hands. She can make muffins that make those two star-crossed lovers get together! She can do this!<br /><br />The plot suffered from obvious issues that didn't get figured out until the end, and obvious bad guys. A lot of the characters were fairly unlikable, including Rose herself. She was SO WHINY. More than that, the plot went exactly where I thought it would go, and of course, it ends on a sort-of cliffhanger to set it up for a series. *Sigh*. It just didn't have all the charm and magic I wanted it to; it felt like it was missing that something special that could really make it magical, which is shame, because I wanted this to be so good.</span>

<div id="review_268116297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268116297" />
    <a title="Bookphile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4792318-bookphile"><img alt="Bookphile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438194146p2/4792318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268116297?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookphile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookphile" href="/user/show/4792318-bookphile">Bookphile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4792318-bookphile?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4792318-bookphile?shelf=amazon-vine">amazon-vine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4792318-bookphile?shelf=children-s-lit">children-s-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4792318-bookphile?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268116297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3353761136320302858">Whew. This one took a long time to finish. It was a really clever idea, but the execution didn't excite me very much. More complete review to come.<br/><br/>Full review:<br/><br/>When I read the premise of Bliss, I was very intrigued. It sounded like such a fun idea: would the temptations of her family's magical bakery prove too much for young Rose Bliss? My daughter and I read the book over the course of several months and, though reading it in short chunks didn't help, it never really captured me the way I might </span>
  <span id="freeText3353761136320302858" style="display:none">Whew. This one took a long time to finish. It was a really clever idea, but the execution didn't excite me very much. More complete review to come.<br /><br />Full review:<br /><br />When I read the premise of Bliss, I was very intrigued. It sounded like such a fun idea: would the temptations of her family's magical bakery prove too much for young Rose Bliss? My daughter and I read the book over the course of several months and, though reading it in short chunks didn't help, it never really captured me the way I might have thought. Minor spoilers to follow.<br /><br />I think the biggest problem with this book is it's far too wordy. It felt to me like there was a lot of filler that could have been trimmed, which would have made it a tighter, more compelling story. Since it's middle grade, I found it kind of odd that it delved into minutiae that struck me as the sort of details only adults might fully be able to appreciate. I know a lot of these things went straight over my daughter's head.<br /><br />What I did like about the novel was Rose. I'm sure most kids can identify with feeling a little invisible at times. The book has some good things to say about the way people tend to fills the roles they're assigned. Rose is seen as the mature, responsible one, and she is, but she chafes under the weight of those expectations. She's likable and sympathetic, yet flawed in a way that makes her seem entirely real. Why wouldn't she find it hard to refuse someone who makes me feel like she exists? I really enjoyed her and thought her character was deftly handled.<br /><br />Another strong point was Rose's relationship with Aunt Lily. Littlewood isn't heavy-handed about presenting Aunt Lily in a very self-serving way, but my daughter picked up on the subtext. We talked a lot about Aunt Lily and whether Rose really saw Lily as she actually was. I liked that she and I were able to dive into a pretty deep analysis of the book, yet in a way that clearly caught my daughter's interest instead of giving her the impression that we were having a literary lecture. <br /><br />Still, there's just something so flat about this book. The recipes are interesting and the little stories accompanying them are fun, but they just never seemed to live up to their potential. Littlewood has something to say about the burdens of having special abilities and whether or not it's always a good idea to use them, and I thought it was all to the good that the recipes had consequences, but I didn't think the writing was quite deft enough to carry the stories. It's missing an essential spark that makes stories like this come to life.<br /><br />While it felt fairly obvious to me that this book was meant to set up a series, I don't plan on coming back to it. It's not a badly done novel, it just wasn't one that really pulled me in. My daughter said she liked it, but she wasn't as excited about it as she has been with some of the other books we've read together, and she took a long hiatus at one point in favor of reading something else--usually a good indication that she's not entirely engaged with a story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3353761136320302858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5189729735155595468" style="display:none">2.5 - 3 stars<br /><br />A 3 had there been a solid conclusion that did not give the impression of an impending sequel and the loose ends that necessitate one.<br /><br />Rosemary Bliss is the underappreciated, low on self-esteem daughter of magical bakers with three siblings.<br /><br />I liked the story, thought it was fun and cute, but it lacked depth, real humor, any sparkle to its prose and worst of all, no conclusion or resolution to Lily's absconding with the magic cookbook. <div id="review_2076627883" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2076627883" />
    <a title="Book Concierge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge"><img alt="Book Concierge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324904606p2/1628041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2076627883?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Book Concierge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Book Concierge" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge">Book Concierge</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062084231" href="/book/show/11595931-bliss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=cooking">cooking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=middle-school">middle-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=concierge">concierge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2076627883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3133258767247098207"><u>From the book jacket</u>: Rosemary Bliss’s family has a secret. It’s the Bliss Cookery Booke – an ancient leather-bound volume of enchanted recipes like Singing Gingersnaps. Rose and her siblings are supposed to keep the Cookery Booke under lock and key while their parents are out of town, but then a m mysterious stranger shows up. “Aunt” Lily rides a motorcycle, wears purple sequins, and whips up exotic dishes for dinner. <br/><br/><u>My reactions</u><br/>Okay, I knew it was a children’s middle-grade book, and I knew it</span>
  <span id="freeText3133258767247098207" style="display:none"><u>From the book jacket</u>: Rosemary Bliss’s family has a secret. It’s the Bliss Cookery Booke – an ancient leather-bound volume of enchanted recipes like Singing Gingersnaps. Rose and her siblings are supposed to keep the Cookery Booke under lock and key while their parents are out of town, but then a m mysterious stranger shows up. “Aunt” Lily rides a motorcycle, wears purple sequins, and whips up exotic dishes for dinner. <br /><br /><u>My reactions</u><br />Okay, I knew it was a children’s middle-grade book, and I knew it involved magic. But still … this was just so awful I don’t even need some Cookies of Truth to write this review.<br /><br />Rose is only eleven, but she is so unsure of herself, so certain she isn’t pretty or clever or (insert positive attribute here), and she bemoans her lack of looks, brains, etc on practically every page! Given her lack of confidence, it’s no wonder that she’s quickly seduced by Aunt Lily’s glamour and flattery. This, of course, makes me wonder why her parents would entrust the key to the special cabinet to Rose – or any of the children, for that matter. Why not just lock it up and take the key with them? Clearly, I’m not the intended audience, but I can’t imagine my nieces and nephews enjoying this either.<br /><br />Still, I admit that some of the unintended results of their experiments were entertaining. So I’ll give it 2 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3133258767247098207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_277415228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277415228" />
    <a title="Vikki VanSickle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6237983-vikki-vansickle"><img alt="Vikki VanSickle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328448636p2/6237983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277415228?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vikki VanSickle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vikki VanSickle" href="/user/show/6237983-vikki-vansickle">Vikki VanSickle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6237983-vikki-vansickle?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277415228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5709322795370558040">This book was fun. It is ultimately a story about family, with some magical hijinx and a hint of coming-of-age story thrown in, which is why it felt classically American to me. It takes place in a small town that seems to exist just outside of the real world, a safe, wholesome place with kooky locals and life lessons to be learned, untouched and nostalgic all at the same time. It’s the kind of place where kids have quirky names-Rosemary, Sage, Parsley (called Leigh) and Thyme (called Ty) and nic</span>
  <span id="freeText5709322795370558040" style="display:none">This book was fun. It is ultimately a story about family, with some magical hijinx and a hint of coming-of-age story thrown in, which is why it felt classically American to me. It takes place in a small town that seems to exist just outside of the real world, a safe, wholesome place with kooky locals and life lessons to be learned, untouched and nostalgic all at the same time. It’s the kind of place where kids have quirky names-Rosemary, Sage, Parsley (called Leigh) and Thyme (called Ty) and niche businesses (such as Borzini’s Nuttery) manage to survive despite a small population.<br /><br />Girls will relate to Rose with her middle grade anxieties. Her brothers were irritating and I found it hard to believe that the Bliss parents let them get away with so much, but then again I never had brothers and as a reader I am supposed to feel what Rose is feeling, which is irritation and injustice. There were moments in Kathryn Littlewood’s prose when I thought, wow, this is a writer to watch! She does a great job getting into the head of a 12 year old girl. At times I got a little bogged down in the silliness of some of the recipes gone awry and at over 350 pages the novel feels a little long, but overall I enjoyed my time with Rose and I think girls aged 8-11 will, too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5709322795370558040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7796427354974674938" style="display:none">Abandoned at p71. Unfortunately the only good thing about this is the cute concept. The execution is disappointing to say the least. The characters don't act or talk like kids should. The internal monologue of the main character is far more repetitive and unsubtle than can be justified by the younger target audience. Just nope.</span>

  <i>3.75/5</i>
</b><br/><br/>Really adorable story about a family who bake stuff infused with magic and the problems that arise when the parents have to travel somewhere for a while. As it's a children's book you can expect entertaining and cute shenanigans.<br/><br/>I would have loved to rate this a bit higher but I had one small issue.   <span id="freeText13155001821191147031" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>3.75/5</i>
</b><br /><br />Really adorable story about a family who bake stuff infused with magic and the problems that arise when the parents have to travel somewhere for a while. As it's a children's book you can expect entertaining and cute shenanigans.<br /><br />I would have loved to rate this a bit higher but I had one small issue. Don't make your main character constantly think about how she isn't pretty and others are and have a conclusion that says that "nice and pretty people" are those you have to be careful of. That's a really stupid thing to teach children. Being pretty shouldn't be a goal but hating people that are is also not something that should be done. And some people are nice and pretty and actually good people. That's basically my only complaint because otherwise the story was adorable.<br /><br />I will definitely continue this series. It's not my favorite kids' book but cute.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1947378676613048826">Rose Bliss knows for sure that her parents aren't ordinary bakers. They mix magic and turn out miracles in the small town of Calamity Falls. No sooner does an urgent matter calls Mr. and Mrs. Bliss away, then a stranger shows up on their front step, claiming to be Aunt Lily. Rose borrows some of her mother's recipes; hilarity ensues. <br/><br/>Muffins and mason jars. Birthmarks and breaking rules. Whisks and worries. Stetson doughnuts and saving the day.   <span id="freeText1947378676613048826" style="display:none">Rose Bliss knows for sure that her parents aren't ordinary bakers. They mix magic and turn out miracles in the small town of Calamity Falls. No sooner does an urgent matter calls Mr. and Mrs. Bliss away, then a stranger shows up on their front step, claiming to be Aunt Lily. Rose borrows some of her mother's recipes; hilarity ensues. <br /><br />Muffins and mason jars. Birthmarks and breaking rules. Whisks and worries. Stetson doughnuts and saving the day. This is a fun read with a quirky cast. I love Purdy's (that'd be Mrs. Bliss's) names for her children. I've always loved stories that bring a family closer together. Can't wait for the next book!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="hanhilhen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="hanhilhen" href="/user/show/1849907-hanhilhen">hanhilhen</a>

<div id="review_1783659051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1783659051" />
    <a title="Josie Funk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19498358-josie-funk"><img alt="Josie Funk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366163442p2/19498358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1783659051?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josie Funk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josie Funk" href="/user/show/19498358-josie-funk">Josie Funk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19498358-josie-funk?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19498358-josie-funk?shelf=middlegrade">middlegrade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19498358-josie-funk?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1783659051&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1783659051" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3409398247262240294">Goodreads steered me wrong with this recommendation. <br/><br/>Reading "Bliss" was a lot like watching a 3rd grade class trying to perform a Shakespeare play. They can follow the script just fine, but their understanding of the characters' motivations and emotions is vastly limited because they lack real-world experience. The result is 8 year old actors announcing "I am sad!" or "That makes me angry!" to the audience; it's very two-dimensional and flat. <br/><br/>And Littlewood does announce to her audience what th</span>
  <span id="freeText3409398247262240294" style="display:none">Goodreads steered me wrong with this recommendation. <br /><br />Reading "Bliss" was a lot like watching a 3rd grade class trying to perform a Shakespeare play. They can follow the script just fine, but their understanding of the characters' motivations and emotions is vastly limited because they lack real-world experience. The result is 8 year old actors announcing "I am sad!" or "That makes me angry!" to the audience; it's very two-dimensional and flat. <br /><br />And Littlewood does announce to her audience what the main character Rose is feeling. Constantly. I would wager that the phrase "Rose felt..." makes up over half the book. Many times, her emotions are displayed purely in the narration, so rather than describing common self-conscious behaviors, such as mumbling, fidgeting, peering through bangs, staring at the floor, etc, the author just informs us, loudly, how Rose feels, in a very Tell-Don't-Show kind of way. The few times there <i>is</i> description, such as 'Rose hung back while her family crowded forward', it's immediately followed by <i>'And she did this because she felt ordinary!'</i> In case you, y'know, forgot. <br /><br />The book does not trust its readers to interpret character's actions at all, and Rose's feelings of inferiority are spelled out like a neon sign and stamped all over the narrative, again and again. It talks down to its readers. Even middle-grade readers, I think, would feel a bit annoyed at being talked down to like this. <br /><br />The book might be more suitable for elementary grade, because of its oversimplified-characters and plot, but I worry that the vocabulary would be too high for some children that young. <br /><br />Anyway, Outside of Rose, the other characters don't feel real, either... more like caricatures. Aunt Lily, who is supposed to be the sophisticated adult, literally says "Wheeeeee!" at one point. Sage, described as 'the funny one' never says anything particularly hilarious. Leigh, who is <i>three</i>, has about the same dialogue types and cadence as everyone else. <br /><br />I feel like Littlewood didn't understand her characters for the majority of the book and was pushing characterization through informed narration. By the end, she seemed to get the hang of it a little, with characters actually acting out their traits instead of just saying them. But that is a sign the book needs to be rewritten, once you as an author finally understand your characters. <br /><br />The magic was a bit of a letdown. The first sentence makes it sound like the magic in the book will be flashy and fantastic, lightning bolts folded into batter. But the rest of the ingredients are pretty ordinary (whispers in a jar, egg from a specific bird) or downright absurd (a tear from a warlock's eye, a dwarf of perpetual sleep who is <i>easily</i> woken up, etc.) Nothing that would make Rose ache to become a magical baker. Not that Rose really sold me on that wish either - I never got the impression that Rose had ever even asked her parents to teach her magic, or that they had ever told her "no". Which pretty much makes the plot of the book moot. <br /><br />Lily is a poor villain. She's meant to be a direct foil to Rose, everything she could be if she chased fame rather than family. But she suffers from the same cardboard-personality that afflicts all the characters. It's pretty obvious from the get-go that she has ulterior motives, yet no one seems to notice or care but Rose, who is pretty certain she shouldn't trust Lily but does anyway, because plot. <br /><br />But because the story refuses to acknowledge that Lily is trying to steal the cookbook, we never really get to see <i>why</i> she wants to be rich and famous; we never get to see any emotion other than greed, manic bubbly-ness, or sweet-talking in her; and we never get backstory beyond a line or two about how she "left her family behind, no biggie." Which, if you're trying to provide contrast between her and Rose, and the importance of Rose's dedication to family, is <i>pretty important.</i> All in all, she becomes less of a cunning villain and a dark reflection of the main character, and just turns into a greedy woman who easily tricks some very trusting children. Not really thrilling for a villain at all. <br /><br />Lastly, the plot was predictable and boring. That's what earned this book a 1-star review from me: the worst sin a story can commit is being boring. I nearly put the book down several times, and I never leave a book unfinished. The magical mishaps all seemed predictable and contrived, and didn't have any immediate, pressing consequences to keep the story rolling forward. <br /><br />Overall, nothing in this book felt REAL to me, and failed to keep my interest. The story would've worked better as a parody, honestly. I felt like this book had a load of potential and it was squandered. If you like it, kudos to you, but I personally won't be hunting down the sequel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3409398247262240294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1212350462" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212350462" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12293609-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399171915p2/12293609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1212350462?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/12293609-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12293609-kate?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12293609-kate?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212350462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17835259721055188546">Rosemary Bliss has always known there was something different about the goods that her parents sell at their bakery. Some of them are ordinary - the carrot-bran muffins, the coconut cakes, the scones. But others... well, Rose just can't shake the thought that they're magical. When she's ten years old, her suspicions are confirmed - her parents have magic in their blood, and can bake cakes that cure illness, cookies that tell the truth, and biscuits that cause the eater to float in the air. Two y</span>
  <span id="freeText17835259721055188546" style="display:none">Rosemary Bliss has always known there was something different about the goods that her parents sell at their bakery. Some of them are ordinary - the carrot-bran muffins, the coconut cakes, the scones. But others... well, Rose just can't shake the thought that they're magical. When she's ten years old, her suspicions are confirmed - her parents have magic in their blood, and can bake cakes that cure illness, cookies that tell the truth, and biscuits that cause the eater to float in the air. Two years later, her parents are called out of town to cure a city of swine flu, leaving Rose and her siblings Leigh, Ty, and Sage (yes, their names really are an eye-roll-worthy homage to Simon and Garfunkel) to guard the Bliss Cookery Booke, holding all the magic recipes. <br /><br />Then Aunt Lily, who they've never met, shows up to babysit and help them run the bakery... but there's just one problem. The kids' parents didn't say anything about Aunt Lily coming to babysit. Or anything about her at all. Rose is itching to try some magical recipes now that she's out from under her parents' thumb. But how can she keep it a secret from "Aunt" Lily? And does she really trust her glamorous relative?<br /><br />I was interested in this one as a read-alike to Lisa Graff's excellent <i>A Tangle of Knots</i>, and found it to be very different from that book. I enjoyed it, but unfortunately found myself skimming toward the end as I quickly figured out that the whole book is basically a set-up for the sequels where Rose will chase down the not-so-secretly evil Lily. There were definitely some plot holes and some headscratchers of decisions from the kids (the biggest being allowing a stranger into their lives based on a birthmark), but children won't mind that at all. <br /><br />I think I'll enjoy the sequels a lot more due to the predictability and sloppy premise of the first book, but Littlewood created a fun cast of characters and a great concept.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17835259721055188546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290715338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2837230755694982946">When Rosemary Bliss’ parents must leave town, responsible daughter, Rose takes over the family bakery, knowing her siblings will not be much help. Young readers will identify with Rose, who feels unappreciated and ordinary in a family whose talents include baking magical pastries and cakes. Rose wants to feel pretty, important, special, and when the previously unheard-of Aunt Lily shows up on a motorcycle right after the Bliss parents leave, Rose is captivated by someone who sees her potential. </span>
  <span id="freeText2837230755694982946" style="display:none">When Rosemary Bliss’ parents must leave town, responsible daughter, Rose takes over the family bakery, knowing her siblings will not be much help. Young readers will identify with Rose, who feels unappreciated and ordinary in a family whose talents include baking magical pastries and cakes. Rose wants to feel pretty, important, special, and when the previously unheard-of Aunt Lily shows up on a motorcycle right after the Bliss parents leave, Rose is captivated by someone who sees her potential. She is also disturbed by Lily and doesn’t completely trust that she is who she says she is.<br /><br />Lily’s arrival sets in motion Rose’s decision to use the magical family cookbook that has heretofore been off limits to her. Chaos ensues as the Bliss kids add magical ingredients to recipes they think their town needs, and much of the book’s sweet humor comes from their misadventures. They bake well, but can’t foresee the consequences of who eats Love Muffins or Cookies of Truth or Turn-Around-Inside-Out-Upside-Down-Cake.<br /><br />Kids will love the comedy that is almost slapstick at times, and Rose’s push-pull of wanting to be special and also, responsible to her parent’s wishes. There’s a smidgen of romance, too, but the story’s heart is in what it means to be a member of a family, and that each person has her own role to play.<br /><br />My guess is we have the start of a series here…<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2837230755694982946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/350111803?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Hay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Hay" href="/user/show/7431260-sarah-hay">Sarah Hay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350111803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6254177756977974911">This one is ok. The Bliss family run a small town bakery where they occasionally offer some magical treats to help their unknowing customers. But, when mom and dad leave the kids in charge with the instructions of 'no magic,' inevitably, chaos ensues.<br/>The book mostly follows Rose who is the second oldest Bliss child, living in the shadow of her charming, athletic, really really good looking older brother. Rose struggles with issues of self esteem because she is not allowed to bake magical recipes</span>
  <span id="freeText6254177756977974911" style="display:none">This one is ok. The Bliss family run a small town bakery where they occasionally offer some magical treats to help their unknowing customers. But, when mom and dad leave the kids in charge with the instructions of 'no magic,' inevitably, chaos ensues.<br />The book mostly follows Rose who is the second oldest Bliss child, living in the shadow of her charming, athletic, really really good looking older brother. Rose struggles with issues of self esteem because she is not allowed to bake magical recipes and she feels that she is rather plain looking, especially compared to her brother. Then she is introduced to her Aunt Lily who could easily pass for a super model. Baking up a few magical recipes helps Rose's confidence, but when things turn sour she begins to despair.<br />There were a few plot twists that seemed left unexplained in this book. For example there is a strange voice in the basement that whispers some to Rose but is never really discussed. I am guessing that this will come up again in the sequel.<br />This is not a bad book for young tweens, probably girls who enjoy a little fantasy with a touch of romance (though there really isn't much, mostly talking about crushes). Might be good to recommend to kids who like Savvy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6254177756977974911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/4756329-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4756329-angie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4756329-angie?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer369856985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer408149447940294739">The Bliss Family Bakery offers wonderful baked treats with a bit of magic. Mr. and Mrs. Bliss are called away to help fight a mysterious flu in a neighboring town and they leave the Bliss children in charge of the bakery. Thyme, Rosemary, Sage and Parsley (Leigh) have varying reactions to being left alone with the bakery to run, but you know that disaster is going to loom. They have one rule...no magic. And of course that just makes the magic that much more tempting. Then comes a mysteries Aunt </span>
  <span id="freeText408149447940294739" style="display:none">The Bliss Family Bakery offers wonderful baked treats with a bit of magic. Mr. and Mrs. Bliss are called away to help fight a mysterious flu in a neighboring town and they leave the Bliss children in charge of the bakery. Thyme, Rosemary, Sage and Parsley (Leigh) have varying reactions to being left alone with the bakery to run, but you know that disaster is going to loom. They have one rule...no magic. And of course that just makes the magic that much more tempting. Then comes a mysteries Aunt Lily into the picture to seduce them all and tempt them with more magic. What follows is magical mayhem.<br /><br />This was a fun, magical story. The Bliss kids all have their own unique personalities that shine throughout the book; although Rose is really our heroine. She is the one that struggles with Lily's seduction, but is very tempted by the magic. I thought the magical mayhem was really fun and a bit crazy. That backwards spell was pretty unusual. However, Lily always seem to play a little one-dimensional to me. Even when she was being nice you always knew she had other motives. The ending wasn't really a surprise after all the set up of Lily being the villain. I think book two should be pretty interesting after the end of this one. Definitely a fun series to watch.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1218372687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5238081792840777389">Bliss is a creative book that will feeds your imagination. The Bliss family owns a magic cook book and serves up magic treats that causes a stir in the town. I personally love baking and magic,so I would say this was a perfect book for me. Other then those to components the book was rather plain. There were times in the book that seemed to drag on and on but on the other hand there are some parts where they just touched on the subject. This book was fun and light hearted being child friendly and</span>
  <span id="freeText5238081792840777389" style="display:none">Bliss is a creative book that will feeds your imagination. The Bliss family owns a magic cook book and serves up magic treats that causes a stir in the town. I personally love baking and magic,so I would say this was a perfect book for me. Other then those to components the book was rather plain. There were times in the book that seemed to drag on and on but on the other hand there are some parts where they just touched on the subject. This book was fun and light hearted being child friendly and was be charming at times. There wasn't much drive to it not making it a page turner for me. I do know that this book is a series and that the story gets better with a more interesting plot like a Grand Prix, baking contest. With that said I am looking forward to the next book since it seems to be more exciting. My friend that loves baking was carrying this book which then lead to me being curios and reading it as well, I wasn't exactly recommended to read this book but I would recommend it to friends that love food. Overall a light book that still was able to charm me with its magical spells.</span>

  <span id="freeText18051602297072431266" style="display:none">Since I read this at the beginning of the month I can't really write a good review, but I can inform you of my opinion on this book.<br />First of all, I seriously loved Ty. He was so funny and sounded really cute and was just a lovable character other than his stupidity. Rose killed me. Most of the time I couldn't stand her character.   <span id="freeText11870558146139298095" style="display:none">Rose's parents run a bakery. But it's not an average bakery. The Bliss family recipes are magic. Her mother's Stone Sleep Snickerdoodle's cured Mr. Rook's sleepwalking and the Fluffy White Macaroons floated Mr. Wadsworth out of the bottom of the well he was trapped in. Rose is the true baker out of the four kids and has always been fascinated with their magical recipes. So when Rose's parents travel off to Humbleton to cure a huge flu outbreak with their almond croissants, she and her siblings can't resist whipping up a few batches to fix the town's inhabitants. They agree they'll keep it a secret, but everything gets more twisted when their mysterious and charming aunt shows up and takes a special interest in the secret Bliss cookbook.<br /><br />This book was part of a post I did all about books that were perfect for any kind of spring break.   <span id="freeText13450360307936633417" style="display:none">Rosemary Bliss thinks she is too plain just the boring, obedient middle child that no one notices.<br /><br />Until one week her parents go away a mystery aunt comes to stay who is everything Rose has every wanted to be. <br /><br />Rose struggles between being obedient, and keeping the family secret and doing what get brothers and Lilly want her to do.<br /><br />This is a must read for any girl middle kid who feels a little too average. In the end it shows that people don't have to single you out to be noticing you. If you are doing good you are being respected and sometimes we might need to check with a parent to reassure ourselves of that. In the end does it matter if people call is funny or pretty all the time! No, but as long as you know what you are that's what matters know how great you are and it won't matter if others realize what your good at.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4211051-akoss?shelf=all-mg">all-mg</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619633946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17049051319241603819">A fun and breezy read that unfortunately isn't exactly memorable.<br/>I loved the concept of bakery mixed with magic and the dramatic consequences of magic practice gone wrong. Some of them were downright funny.<br/>However Rose's serious lack of self esteem became a bit bothersome and her siblings were a bit typical in their behaviors. They only acted out of character to make the plot advance.<br/>Aunt Lily was in my opinion the only outstanding character. She kept me guessing until the end. I knew she was up</span>
  <span id="freeText17049051319241603819" style="display:none">A fun and breezy read that unfortunately isn't exactly memorable.<br />I loved the concept of bakery mixed with magic and the dramatic consequences of magic practice gone wrong. Some of them were downright funny.<br />However Rose's serious lack of self esteem became a bit bothersome and her siblings were a bit typical in their behaviors. They only acted out of character to make the plot advance.<br />Aunt Lily was in my opinion the only outstanding character. She kept me guessing until the end. I knew she was up to something but she played it in a sleek way.<br />However the way the book ended was off and I can't really discuss it without spoilers.<br /><br />If you are looking for a fun and light book this will definitely do the job. The writing is smooth and casual. I was thoroughly entertained.</span>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!

    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('htzwiNl+vNY/f55k2atKyefQgx0ZSUENYsdZmhh++GKtccrGJ/n84y1KQ4iPETekV8PLkI4rvCyhPkD37Ny6BQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iwrqJ6sm07fJ4MtUVAiMkmHm+pi+64U+1pDOsLeukNugp9BpVaGTgtvVFrgCsvH/0fWyFSmJeB8VadfdQwzSvA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7911875415422286439">Kathryn Littlewood is a writer, actress, comedienne, and bon vivant who lives in New York City, works often in Los Angeles, and has a sweet tooth for pain au chocolat and sweet novels for middle-grade readers. This, her second novel, is a sequel to her first, Bliss. </span>
